But we can check: In our coordinate setup, we computed P's x-coordinate. We can compute the line through A and P: AP. We can also compute the orthocenter H of triangle PMN. Let's compute H coordinates.

Given triangle PMN, we have coordinates: P = (x_P, y_P) (we'll compute), M = (0,0), N = (c,0). So MN is horizontal. Therefore, the altitude from P is vertical line through P: x = x_P. The altitude from M is line through M perpendicular to PN. The altitude from N is line through N perpendicular to PM. The orthocenter H is intersection of altitudes. Since MN horizontal, altitude from P is vertical. So H has x-coordinate = x_P. So H = (x_P, y_H) where y_H is the y-coordinate of intersection of vertical line x=x_P with altitude from M (or N). So we can compute y_H using the altitude from M: line through M (0,0) perpendicular to PN. So we need slope of PN: (y_P - 0)/(x_P - c) = y_P/(x_P - c). So slope of perpendicular = -(x_P - c)/y_P. Equation: y = - (x_P - c)/y_P * x. At x = x_P, y = - (x_P - c)/y_P * x_P = - x_P(x_P - c)/y_P. So H = (x_P, - x_P(x_P - c)/y_P). That's one expression.

Alternatively, we could compute using altitude from N: line through N(c,0) perpendicular to PM. Slope of PM: (y_P - 0)/(x_P - 0) = y_P/x_P. So perpendicular slope = -x_P/y_P. Equation: y = -x_P/y_P (x - c). At x = x_P, y = -x_P/y_P (x_P - c) = - x_P(x_P - c)/y_P. Same.

So H = (x_P, - x_P(x_P - c)/y_P).

Now we need line through H parallel to AP. So direction vector of AP: from A to P: P - A. So â„“: passes through H with direction (P - A). We need to prove that â„“ is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF. So we need to show that the distance from the circumcenter of BEF to â„“ equals the radius, or that the power of some point is zero and line is perpendicular to radius, etc.

Better: Show that â„“ is the polar of some point with respect to circle (BEF), or that â„“ is the radical axis of two circles that are tangent? Alternatively, we can try to compute the equation of circle (BEF) and show that â„“ has exactly one intersection with it. That is a computational approach.

x0 = (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2c)

We can simplify numerator: (2cr)^2 - (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)^2 = (2cr - (c^2+r^2-R^2))(2cr + (c^2+r^2-R^2)) = (2cr - c^2 - r^2 + R^2)(2cr + c^2 + r^2 - R^2) = (R^2 - (c^2 -2cr + r^2))((c^2+2cr+r^2) - R^2) = (R^2 - (c-r)^2)((c+r)^2 - R^2) = (R - (c-r))(R + (c-r))((c+r)-R)((c+r)+R) = (R - c + r)(R + c - r)(c+r - R)(c+r+R)

Thus y0^2 = ((R - c + r)(R + c - r)(c+r-R)(c+r+R))/(4c^2). Since circles intersect, all factors positive. Note that R - c + r >0? Because c < R+r => R - c + r >0? Actually, c < R+r => R - c + r >0? x_P = (c+R - r)s / (2s) = (c+R - r)/2

So x_P = (c+R - r)/2. Nice! So P's x-coordinate is simply (c+R - r)/2. That is a clean expression.

We have:
vآ·d = (A-N)آ·P - r^2 + c u.

Thus, t_E = -2 (A-M)آ·d / |d|^2.

Similarly, for خ“: center N=(n,0), radius R_خ“. Since A is on خ“, |A-N|^2 = R_خ“^2. So t_F = -2 (A-N)آ·d / |d|^2.

Now, compute (A-M)آ·d. A=(0,a), M=(m,0), so A-M = (-m, a). d = (P_x, P_y - a). So (A-M)آ·d = -m P_x + a(P_y - a) = -m P_x + a P_y - a^2.

We also have P_y = a(m-P_x)/(R_خ©+m). So a P_y = a^2 (m-P_x)/(R_خ©+m). Then -m P_x + a P_y - a^2 = -m P_x + a^2 (m-P_x)/(R_خ©+m) - a^2 = -m P_x + a^2 (m-P_x - (R_خ©+m))/(R_خ©+m) = -m P_x + a^2 ( -P_x - R_خ©)/(R_خ©+m) = -m P_x - a^2 (P_x+R_خ©)/(R_خ©+m). Given the complexity, perhaps we can find a more clever synthetic proof. Since the problem is from an IMO or similar, there must be a synthetic solution. Let's think about the configuration.

We have circles خ© and خ“ intersecting at A and B. Let O be the circumcenter of triangle PMN. Since P is circumcenter of ACD, and M,N are centers of خ©,خ“. The orthocenter H of triangle PMN is such that PH âں‚ MN, MH âں‚ PN, NH âں‚ PM.

Given the difficulty, I'll attempt to prove the tangency condition using coordinates but with a clever parametrization that reduces the algebra. For instance, we can set up a coordinate system where the common chord AB is the y-axis, and the line of centers is the x-axis. Then we have A=(0,a), B=(0,-a), M=(m,0), N=(n,0) with m<n. Then we have r^2 = m^2+a^2, R^2 = n^2+a^2. Then we can compute P as circumcenter of ACD. Points: C=(m-R,0) because C is intersection of خ© with x-axis left of M: distance from M to C = R, so C = (m-R,0). Similarly, D=(n+R,0). So P_x = (m-R + n+R)/2 = (m+n)/2. So P_x = (m+n)/2. And P_y is from condition |P-A| = |P-C|. Let's compute that.

We have A=(0,a), C=(m-R,0). Then P=( (m+n)/2, y). Then |P-A|^2 = ((m+n)/2)^2 + (y-a)^2. |P-C|^2 = ((m+n)/2 - (m-R))^2 + y^2 = ((m+n)/2 - m + R)^2 + y^2 = ((n-m)/2 + R)^2 + y^2. Set equal:

((m+n)/2)^2 + (y-a)^2 = ((n-m)/2 + R)^2 + y^2
=> ((m+n)/2)^2 + y^2 -2ay + a^2 = ((n-m)/2)^2 + 2R*(n-m)/2 + R^2) + y^2 = ((n-m)/2)^2 + R(n-m) + R^2 + y^2
=> ((m+n)/2)^2 -2ay + a^2 = ((n-m)/2)^2 + R(n-m) + R^2
=> ((m+n)^2 - (n-m)^2)/4 -2ay + a^2 = R(n-m) + R^2
=> ( (m^2+2mn+n^2) - (n^2-2mn+m^2) )/4 -2ay + a^2 = R(n-m) + R^2
=> (4mn)/4 -2ay + a^2 = R(n-m) + R^2
=> mn -2ay + a^2 = R(n-m) + R^2
=> -2ay = R(n-m) + R^2 - mn - a^2
=> 2ay = mn + a^2 - R(n-m) - R^2
=> y = (mn + a^2 - R(n-m) - R^2)/(2a)

Now, note that R^2 = n^2+a^2, so R^2 = n^2+a^2. Then:

mn + a^2 - R(n-m) - (n^2+a^2) = mn - n^2 - R(n-m) = n(m-n) - R(n-m) = -n(n-m) - R(n-m) = -(n+m)(n-m) = -(n^2-m^2). So y = -(n^2-m^2)/(2a). Thus, P_y = -(n^2-m^2)/(2a). This is negative since n>m. So P = ((m+n)/2, -(n^2-m^2)/(2a)).

Now, we also have H = orthocenter of triangle PMN. Points: P=( (m+n)/2, -(n^2-m^2)/(2a) ), M=(m,0), N=(n,0). Since MN horizontal, altitude from P is vertical line x = (m+n)/2. Altitude from M: line through M perpendicular to PN. Compute vector PN = N - P = (n - (m+n)/2, 0 - (-(n^2-m^2)/(2a)) = ((n-m)/2, (n^2-m^2)/(2a)) = ((n-m)/2, (n-m)(n+m)/(2a)) = (n-m)(1/2, (n+m)/(2a)). So slope of PN = (n^2-m^2)/(2a) / ((n-m)/2) = (n-m)(n+m)/(2a) * (2/(n-m)) = (n+m)/a. So perpendicular slope = -a/(n+m). So altitude from M: through M(m,0) with slope -a/(n+m). Equation: y = (-a/(n+m))(x-m). At x = (m+n)/2, y = (-a/(n+m))((m+n)/2 - m) = (-a/(n+m))((n-m)/2) = -a(n-m)/(2(n+m)). So H = ( (m+n)/2, -a(n-m)/(2(n+m)) ). Since n>m, H is below x-axis. Good.

Now, line AP: A=(0,a), P=((m+n)/2, -(n^2-m^2)/(2a)). So direction d = P - A = ((m+n)/2, -(n^2-m^2)/(2a) - a) = ((m+n)/2, -(n^2-m^2 + 2a^2)/(2a)). Compute n^2-m^2 = (n-m)(n+m). And 2a^2 = 2a^2. So d = ((m+n)/2, -( (n-m)(n+m) + 2a^2 )/(2a) ). But we also have that (n-m)(n+m) = n^2-m^2. So d = ((m+n)/2, -(n^2-m^2+2a^2)/(2a)).

Now, we need E and F as second intersections of line AP with خ© and خ“.

Equation: y - y0/2 = - (x0 - c - R)/y0 * (x - (x0 + c + R)/2)

Now P is intersection of these two lines. We can solve for x-coordinate.

Letâ€™s denote:

Line1: y = y0/2 - (x0 + r)/y0 * (x - (x0 - r)/2)
Line2: y = y0/2 - (x0 - c - R)/y0 * (x - (x0 + c + R)/2)

Set equal:

y0/2 - (x0 + r)/y0 * (x - (x0 - r)/2) = y0/2 - (x0 - c - R)/y0 * (x - (x0 + c + R)/2)

Cancel y0/2, multiply by y0:

- (x0 + r) * (x - (x0 - r)/2) = - (x0 - c - R) * (x - (x0 + c + R)/2)

Multiply both sides by -1:

(x0 + r) * (x - (x0 - r)/2) = (x0 - c - R) * (x - (x0 + c + R)/2)

Now expand:

Left: (x0 + r)x - (x0 + r)(x0 - r)/2 = (x0 + r)x - (x0^2 - r^2)/2
Right: (x0 - c - R)x - (x0 - c - R)(x0 + c + R)/2 = (x0 - c - R)x - ((x0)^2 - (c+R)^2)/2

Thus:

(x0 + r)x - (x0^2 - r^2)/2 = (x0 - c - R)x - (x0^2 - (c+R)^2)/2

Bring terms:

(x0 + r - x0 + c + R)x = (x0^2 - r^2)/2 - (x0^2 - (c+R)^2)/2

Simplify left: (r + c + R)x
Right: [ (x0^2 - r^2) - (x0^2 - (c+R)^2) ] /2 = [ -r^2 + (c+R)^2 ]/2 = [ (c+R)^2 - r^2 ]/2

Thus:

(r + c + R)x = ((c+R)^2 - r^2)/2 = ((c+R - r)(c+R + r))/2

Hence:

x = ((c+R - r)(c+R + r)) / (2(r + c + R))

Note that (c+R + r) = (r + c + R) = denominator? Actually denominator is 2(r + c + R). So:

x = ((c+R - r)(c+R + r)) / (2(r + c + R)) = ((c+R)^2 - r^2) / (2(r + c + R))

But also note that (c+R)^2 - r^2 = (c+R - r)(c+R + r). So:

x = ((c+R - r)(c+R + r)) / (2(r + c + R)) = (c+R - r)(c+R + r) / (2(r + c + R))

We can simplify: (c+R + r) = (r + c + R). So:

x = (c+R - r) * (c+R + r) / (2(r + c + R)) = (c+R - r)/2 * (c+R + r)/(r + c + R) = (c+R - r)/2 * (c+R + r)/(r + c + R)

Given the analytic setup, we can compute everything in terms of c, r, R. It might simplify nicely.

Letâ€™s compute x0 and y0 explicitly. Use:

x0 = (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2c)
y0^2 = r^2 - x0^2 = r^2 - (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)^2/(4c^2) = (4c^2 r^2 - (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)^2)/(4c^2)

Thus y0^2 = ((R - c + r)(R + c - r)(c+r-R)(c+r+R))/(4c^2). Since circles intersect, all factors positive. Note that R - c + r >0? Because c < R+r => R - c + r >0? Actually, c < R+r => R - c + r >0? Now compute P = (x_P, y_P). We already have x_P = ((c+R)^2 - r^2)/(2(r + c + R)). Let's compute that expression.

So x_P = (c+R - r)/2. Nice! So P's x-coordinate is simply (c+R - r)/2. That is a clean expression.

Now compute y_P. We have line1: y = y0/2 - (x0 + r)/y0 * (x - (x0 - r)/2). At x = x_P. So we need (x_P - (x0 - r)/2). Compute x_P - (x0 - r)/2 = (c+R - r)/2 - (x0 - r)/2 = (c+R - r - x0 + r)/2 = (c+R - x0)/2.

Now compute y0^2 and (x0+r)(c+R-x0). Let's compute both in terms of c,r,R.

First, compute x0 = (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2c). Then x0 + r = (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2c) + r = (c^2 + r^2 - R^2 + 2cr)/(2c) = (c^2 + 2cr + r^2 - R^2)/(2c) = ((c+r)^2 - R^2)/(2c). Actually, compute: 2cr - (c^2+r^2-R^2) = 2cr - c^2 - r^2 + R^2 = R^2 - (c^2 -2cr + r^2) = R^2 - (c-r)^2. And 2cr + (c^2+r^2-R^2) = c^2+2cr+r^2 - R^2 = (c+r)^2 - R^2. Now we have AP line: param A + t*(P-A). We'll find E and F as second intersections with خ© and خ“.

First, find intersection of line AP with خ©: circle centered at M=(0,0) radius r. Solve for t such that |A + t*(P-A)|^2 = r^2. Since A is on خ© (|A|=r), we have A satisfies. So the other intersection E corresponds to t = t_E such that A + t_E*(P-A) = E. The quadratic in t: |A + t d|^2 = r^2, where d = P-A. Since |A|^2 = r^2, we have:

|A|^2 + 2t (Aآ·d) + t^2 |d|^2 = r^2 => 2t (Aآ·d) + t^2 |d|^2 = 0 => t(2 Aآ·d + t |d|^2) = 0. So t=0 gives A; the other t = -2 (Aآ·d)/|d|^2.

Thus E = A + t_E d, with t_E = -2 (Aآ·d)/|d|^2.

Similarly, for خ“: center N=(c,0), radius R. We have A on خ“, so |A - N|^2 = R^2. Let d same. Solve |A - N + t d|^2 = R^2. Let v = A - N. Then |v|^2 = R^2. So:

|v|^2 + 2t (vآ·d) + t^2 |d|^2 = R^2 => 2t (vآ·d) + t^2 |d|^2 = 0 => t=0 or t = -2 (vآ·d)/|d|^2. So F = A + t_F d, with t_F = -2 (vآ·d)/|d|^2.

Thus we can compute E and F coordinates in terms of A, d, and N.

In particular, if we can show that H lies on the polar of something, or that the circle (BEF) is orthogonal to something? Now we need a rigorous proof. We can use analytic geometry with coordinates as above, but we need to show that the distance from O (circumcenter of BEF) to line â„“ equals the radius of (BEF). That is an algebraic identity. Given the complexity, we can simplify by using coordinates and symbolic manipulation, but we must present it as a proof. Since the problem is from an olympiad, a synthetic proof is expected, but we can produce an analytic proof that is rigorous and complete. However, we must ensure that we don't rely on numerical evidence; we need to derive the result algebraically.

We can set up coordinates as we did: M=(0,0), N=(c,0) with c>0, r<R, and define u, v as above. Then compute P, H, E, F, and then O_BEF. Thus, we have two linear equations in O_y and Oآ·d. Letâ€™s denote:

2v X + t_E Y = 0
2v X + t_F Y = (R^2 - r^2)/2

Subtract: (t_F - t_E) Y = (R^2 - r^2)/2 => Y = (R^2 - r^2)/(2(t_F - t_E)). Then X = -t_E Y/(2v) = -t_E (R^2 - r^2)/(4v(t_F - t_E)). So O_y = X, and Oآ·d = Y. But we also need the x-coordinate of O. That is an algebraic identity. Since we have expressions for O_y, Oآ·d, and O_x? Perhaps we can compute O-B vector. Given the time, I'll adopt an analytic approach with coordinates and present a rigorous proof. I'll need to derive the expressions for O and then verify the tangency condition. However, the algebra might be heavy, but we can simplify by using the fact that we have many symmetries and that the expressions for t_E and t_F can be found in terms of distances. Also, we can compute O using the fact that the circumcenter of BEF is the intersection of perpendicular bisectors. But we already have a way to compute O_y and Oآ·d. We also need O_x. From Oآ·d = O_x dx + O_y dy, we can solve for O_x. So O_x = (Oآ·d - O_y dy)/dx. So we can get O_x. Then we can compute the cross product (O-H) أ— d = (O_x - H_x)dy - (O_y - H_y)dx? Given the time, I'll try to produce an analytic solution that is manageable by using the expressions we have for t_E and t_F in terms of PA^2, and then computing O and the tangency condition, and simplifying using the relations that u^2+v^2=r^2 and (u-c)^2+v^2=R^2. We can treat u and v as variables subject to these two equations. Then we can eliminate v^2 = r^2-u^2 and also (u-c)^2 + v^2 = R^2 => (u-c)^2 + r^2-u^2 = R^2 => u^2 -2cu + c^2 + r^2 - u^2 = R^2 => -2cu + c^2 + r^2 = R^2 => 2cu = c^2 + r^2 - R^2 => u = (c^2+r^2-R^2)/(2c). So u is determined by c,r,R. So we can treat u as a known function. Then v = sqrt(r^2-u^2). So we have explicit expressions. So we can compute everything in terms of c, r, R. That might be simpler: we can compute P, H, d, t_E, t_F, E, F, O, and then verify the tangency condition algebraically. This is a polynomial identity in c, r, R. We can do that by hand with careful algebra.

Let's do that. Set:

c = distance between centers (positive). r < R, and circles intersect: |R-r| < c < R+r.

Define u = (c^2 + r^2 - R^2)/(2c)
v = sqrt(r^2 - u^2). We'll keep v symbolic but we can also write v^2 = r^2 - u^2.

Now, compute خ± = c+R-r, خ² = c+r-R, خ³ = c+r+R.

We have:
P_x = خ±/2
P_y = -خ±(u+r)/(2v) = -خ±(u+r)/(2v)

Now, compute dx = P_x - u = خ±/2 - u = (c+R-r)/2 - (c^2+r^2-R^2)/(2c) = (c(c+R-r) - (c^2+r^2-R^2))/(2c) = (c^2 + cR - cr - c^2 - r^2 + R^2)/(2c) = (cR - cr - r^2 + R^2)/(2c) = (R(c-r) + (R^2-r^2))/(2c) = (R(c-r) + (R-r)(R+r))/(2c) = ((R-r)(c+r) + (R-r)(R+r)? Actually, (R^2-r^2)=(R-r)(R+r). So numerator = R(c-r) + (R-r)(R+r) = R(c-r) + (R-r)(R+r). Factor (R-r): (R-r)(R+r) + R(c-r) = (R-r)(R+r) + R(c-r). Not a common factor. But we can also write dx = (R-r)(c+R)/(2c). Let's verify: (R-r)(c+R) = (R-r)c + (R-r)R = cR - cr + R^2 - rR. That is cR - cr + R^2 - rR. Compare to numerator we had: cR - cr - r^2 + R^2. They differ by -r^2 + rR? Actually, (R-r)(c+R) = cR - cr + R^2 - rR. While we have numerator = cR - cr - r^2 + R^2. So they are equal only if -rR = -r^2? That would require R=r. So my earlier expression for dx = (R-r)(c+R)/(2c) is wrong. Let's re-derive: dx = خ±/2 - u = (c+R-r)/2 - (c^2+r^2-R^2)/(2c) = (c(c+R-r) - (c^2+r^2-R^2))/(2c) = (c^2 + cR - cr - c^2 - r^2 + R^2)/(2c) = (cR - cr - r^2 + R^2)/(2c) = (R(c-r) + (R^2 - r^2))/(2c) = (R(c-r) + (R-r)(R+r))/(2c). Now, factor (R-r): (R-r)(R+r) + R(c-r) = (R-r)(R+r) + R(c-r). Not a simple product. But we can also write: (R(c-r) + (R^2-r^2)) = (R(c-r) + (R-r)(R+r)) = (R(c-r) + (R-r)(R+r)). There is a known formula: If we have points B, E, F, then the circumcenter O is given by:

O = ( (|B|^2 (E-F) + |E|^2 (F-B) + |F|^2 (B-E) ) / (2 * (B أ— (E-F) + E أ— (F-B) + F أ— (B-E)) )? Actually, in vector form, the circumcenter can be expressed as:

The denominator is a scalar (the area of triangle times 2), and numerator is a vector. So that is a formula. However, we need to compute cross products, which are determinants. This might be doable with symbolic algebra.

Let's use the vector formula for circumcenter in terms of barycentric coordinates. For triangle with vertices X, Y, Z, the circumcenter is given by:

O = ( (|X|^2 (Y-Z) + |Y|^2 (Z-X) + |Z|^2 (X-Y) ) / (2 * (X أ— (Y-Z) + Y أ— (Z-X) + Z أ— (X-Y)) )? Actually, the denominator is the scalar (2 * area * something). The formula is:

Set:
B = (u, -v)
E = (u + t_E dx, v + t_E dy)
F = (u + t_F dx, v + t_F dy)

Then we can compute |B|^2 = u^2+v^2 = r^2.
|E|^2 = (u + t_E dx)^2 + (v + t_E dy)^2 = u^2+v^2 + 2t_E(ux+vy) + t_E^2(x^2+y^2) = r^2 + 2t_E(ux+vy) + t_E^2 PA^2.
But ux+vy = u dx + v dy? Since A=(u,v), and d=(dx,dy), so ux+vy = u(dx)+v(dy) = Aآ·d = -rخ³/2. So |E|^2 = r^2 + 2t_E*(-rخ³/2) + t_E^2 PA^2 = r^2 - t_E rخ³ + t_E^2 PA^2.
Similarly, |F|^2 = r^2 - t_F rخ³ + t_F^2 PA^2.

Now, we need to compute the vector numerator: N = r^2 (E-F) + |E|^2 (F-B) + |F|^2 (B-E). This is a vector. And denominator D = 2 * ( B أ— (E-F) + E أ— (F-B) + F أ— (B-E) )? Actually, the formula is:

We can compute the denominator: Den = 2 * ( B أ— (E-F) + E أ— (F-B) + F أ— (B-E) ). But note that the sum of these cross products is equal to 2 * (area of triangle BEF) times something? Actually, for any triangle with vertices X, Y, Z, the sum X أ— (Y-Z) + Y أ— (Z-X) + Z أ— (X-Y) = 2 * area (with sign). So that sum is 2 * area. So Den = 2 * (2 * area) = 4 * area. So Den = 4 * area(BEF). So that is a scalar.

Thus, O = N / (4 * area). So O is the vector N divided by 4 times the area.

Given the time, I think it's best to produce a solution that uses coordinates and then simplifies using the relationships we have. I'll present the proof as follows:

1. Place the configuration in a coordinate system with M=(0,0), N=(1,0) after scaling MN=1. Let A=(u,v) with v>0, so that u=(1+r^2-R^2)/2, v=âˆڑ(r^2-u^2). Then B=(u,-v).
